  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2181346679" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2181346679" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23315273-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546293743p2/23315273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2181346679?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/23315273-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780393338416" href="/book/show/7280651-audition">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23315273-carol?shelf=japan">japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23315273-carol?shelf=horror-gothic">horror-gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23315273-carol?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23315273-carol?shelf=not-united-states">not-united-states</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23315273-carol?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23315273-carol?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23315273-carol?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2181346679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16485750481573361806">Murakami doesn't believe in boundaries, so if you expect an author to pull his punches, keep on moving past Audition. From maybe the tenth page forward, it's clear that no good will come of the obsession Aoyama, a Tokyo-based, widowed documentary film-maker and father to Shige, his teen son, develops for Yamasaki, the lovely, elegant and single former-ballet dancer with a troubled childhood. The elaborate set-up of fake auditions Aoyama and his best friend, Yoshikawa devise seems to forecast tha</span>
  <span id="freeText16485750481573361806" style="display:none">Murakami doesn't believe in boundaries, so if you expect an author to pull his punches, keep on moving past Audition. From maybe the tenth page forward, it's clear that no good will come of the obsession Aoyama, a Tokyo-based, widowed documentary film-maker and father to Shige, his teen son, develops for Yamasaki, the lovely, elegant and single former-ballet dancer with a troubled childhood. The elaborate set-up of fake auditions Aoyama and his best friend, Yoshikawa devise seems to forecast that the cause of Yamasaki's ultimate vengeance will be the morally questionable nature of the auditions, but the initial manner of Aoyama's and Yamasaki's introduction turns out to have zero relevance to subsequent events. The only thing that matters is that they meet and Aoyama allow his besottedness to blind him to common sense and Yoshikawa's reasonable cautionary advice. I shook my head multiple times in disbelief until he redeemed himself <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[with his brilliant move with the remote control. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Every scene between Aoyama and Yamasaki is dripping with suspense. Actually, every scene after they meet seems perilous, even when Yamasaki isn't present. It's not a case of if she'll flip out but when and how. And yet. Murakami is a master of suspense. He doesn't introduce distractions or humor to let the reader breathe. Every character is fully realized and authentic. You know who the bad guy is and who the victim is for the entire book and yet are driven to turn the next page and the next in order to see exactly how this will play out and if anyone will survive. Murakami is one of the few writers where the reader accepts that it's entirely possible that all characters will die. He's all in. Always. Read this when you have time to finish it in one sitting.<br /><br />A warning for readers not familiar with Ryu Murakami, however, is in order. If you thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10614.Misery" title="Misery by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Misery</a> was dismayingly violent, Audition isn't for you. Nothing in Murakami's catalog is. <br /><br />For dog lovers: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The dog dies at the end. It's brutal but over quickly. I customarily read no books where a dog dies or an animal is tortured, but in this instance, it's not a heart-rending scene because I didn't get attached to the dog and IMO not a reason to avoid the book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="16485750481573361806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

Wouldn't it be cool to meet a decent girl for a change? One who isn't a total ditz or narcissist, just someone to cuddle and read books with, a girl who's sweet and kind and doesn't insist on <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[cutting off my feet? <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></i> That's when I got the idea to hold an audition for the role of my perfect mate, figuring this would be the surest way t</span>
  <span id="freeText7986684756312590298" style="display:none">Ya know, just the the other day I was walking down the street, thinking to myself, <i>why is it so dang hard to meet nice women these days? Wouldn't it be cool to meet a decent girl for a change? One who isn't a total ditz or narcissist, just someone to cuddle and read books with, a girl who's sweet and kind and doesn't insist on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[cutting off my feet? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></i> That's when I got the idea to hold an audition for the role of my perfect mate, figuring this would be the surest way to find exactly what I was looking for. But then I read this book and decided to swear off women altogether. Like for good.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385796i/744865._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know that girl everyone warned you about? The one you insisted on getting involved with anyway? But dammmmn is she fine, and I'm sure she's totally harmless, and, well (alright little head, you win)...<br><br>I usually don't do this, but I'm going to review <i>Audition</i> in comparison to <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0235198/?ref_=sr_1" rel="nofollow noopener">the film version</a>, which the author reputedly loved so much he specifically requested the same director to adapt his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14289.Coin_Locker_Babies" rel="nofollow noopener">Coin Locker Babies</a> as well. Unfortunately, that project never saw the light of day, because it's clear why Murakami dug the film as much as he did â somehow it manages to remain faithful to his vision, while at the same time improving on it in significant ways. Beyond the superb acting, direction, and cinematography that perfectly captures all the physical/psychological horror he set out to portray in print, Takashi's celluloid adaptation makes up for some of the book's weaknesses as well. As just one example, what many readers would consider to be an abrupt ending on paper is drawn out to great length on screen, quite possibly giving us even more than we bargained for.<br><br>Also (as I may have mentioned before), Eihi Shiina is smoking hot in her portrayal of the book's demure, seemingly innocent sex bomb of a villain. Kinda makes me wanna take up women again, actually... Maybe holding that audition isn't such a bad idea after all?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385796i/744866._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Boy, she's a looker, ain't she? Let's see... Yamasaki Asami, age 24. Bust 82 cm, waist 54 cm, hips 86 cm. Interests include music, dance, and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[not cutting off your feet. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Yup, I'd say this might be the one!<br><br>I'm giving this book 4 stars, rounded up to 5 in light of the superb film adaptation and Murakami's sense in embracing it. So shoot me if you must, just don't <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[cut off my fucking feet! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385796i/744867.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She looks so happy, doesn't she? Well, if you've somehow managed to make it through this entire review without peeping any of the spoilers, congrats â let's see if you can resist peeping her POV <a href="http://www.slashingthrough.com/images/reviews/audition2.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br><br>Aww hell, who am I kidding? I knew you were all too sick to resist â watch the entire gory scene <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YCCW-joMoyY" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6226134799590438808">When I was in my teens and twenties, you could put me in a room of 1000 men and I would undoubtedly gravitate toward the most damaged ones. I guess Aoyama and I have that in common.<br/><br/>The gist of the story is this: Aoyama is a widower who has decided it is time to remarry. Enlisting the help of a filmmaker friend, he holds an audition to find his future wife by duping women into thinking they are auditioning for a film. Out of over a thousand applicants, Aoyama narrows the pool down to a small grou</span>
  <span id="freeText6226134799590438808" style="display:none">When I was in my teens and twenties, you could put me in a room of 1000 men and I would undoubtedly gravitate toward the most damaged ones. I guess Aoyama and I have that in common.<br /><br />The gist of the story is this: Aoyama is a widower who has decided it is time to remarry. Enlisting the help of a filmmaker friend, he holds an audition to find his future wife by duping women into thinking they are auditioning for a film. Out of over a thousand applicants, Aoyama narrows the pool down to a small group of women who will be invited to come in to try out for the role. But before the interviews take place, Aoyama has already fallen for the beautiful Yamasaki Asami based solely on her application. Little does he know, Yamasaki has a dark and horrifying pastâ¦<br /><br />At just under two-hundred pages, this book could easily be read in one sitting. It will grab hold of you and keep you in suspense right through to the very end. Murakamiâs novel reminds us that terrifying things can happen any time; danger is always lurking around the corner. Of course with a short novel such as this there isnât much room for character development, but Murakami does an excellent job of packing a lot of depth into a tiny box. And the ending is a bit abrupt, but I donât really think the story would benefit from dragging out the inevitable. If you are looking for a page turner that will scare the pants off of you, you really canât go wrong with this one.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3264801121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3264801121" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3264801121?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=the-japanese">the-japanese</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=book-to-film">book-to-film</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3264801121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3605362535023185935"><b>âNice person, bad person--thatâs not the level this girl is at. I can see youâre crazy about her and probably wonât be able to hear this, Ao-chan, but I think youâd be better off staying away from someone like her. I canât read her exactly, but I can tell you sheâs either a saint or a monster. Maybe both extremes at once, but not somewhere in between.â</b><br/><br/>Aoyama never remarried after losing his wife to illness. He decided to raise his son by himself, but now seven years later, his son Shige is encou</span>
  <span id="freeText3605362535023185935" style="display:none"><b>âNice person, bad person--thatâs not the level this girl is at. I can see youâre crazy about her and probably wonât be able to hear this, Ao-chan, but I think youâd be better off staying away from someone like her. I canât read her exactly, but I can tell you sheâs either a saint or a monster. Maybe both extremes at once, but not somewhere in between.â</b><br /><br />Aoyama never remarried after losing his wife to illness. He decided to raise his son by himself, but now seven years later, his son Shige is encouraging his Dad to remarry. Aoyama isnât opposed to the idea, and when his friend, a movie producer, suggests having a casting call to find the perfect woman for him, he goes along with the unorthodox idea. <br /><br />An essay, accompanying an application written by one of the hopeful actresses, especially catches his eye. <i>âIt so happens that I studied ballet for many years but had to stop when, at eighteen, I injured my hip. I donât suppose I really had what it takes to become a âprimaâ in any case. But the injury occurred just as I was making preparations to enroll at a ballet school in London, and it felt like the end of the world. It took me years to recover from this disappointment. At the risk of sounding overly dramatic, it was a process not unlike learning to accept death.â</i>So before they even start the tedious process of interviewing all the potential applicants, Aoyama has already decided that Yamasaki Asami is the one for him. <br /><br />She is young and beautiful, but has been tempered by pain and loss which lends an air of melancholy and maturity to her that makes her more attractive to an older man seeking a true companion rather than an adornment. As he begins to take her out for âdates,â he sees those creative attributes that he loved about his wife inherently displayed in Yamasaki Asami. <br /><br />There are niggling concerns. Her stories about herself are vague and do not stand up to even casual scrutiny. She is evasive, a ghost of her past, whenever Aoyama asks personal questions. Not that he needs to know much more about her. He has already made her the heroine of his future life. <br /><br />So this is definitely a slow burn, which seems like a funny thing to say about a book that barely edges 200 pages. I have read several of Ryu Murakamiâs books, and so I kept thinking to myself, when is his odd, sometimes demented, mind going to show itself? I felt the same way when I was watching <i>The Hateful Eight</i>... okay, when is Quentin Tarantinoâs lust to shock going to take over the movie? Needless to say, just as Tarantino shows up in the final part of <i>The Hateful Eight,</i> Murakami also shows up in the final pages of <i>Audition</i>.<br /><br />The true horror of the situation is that Aoyama has been miscast in his role as the villian. He may not be perfect, but he is far from the insidious man that Yamasaki Asami must believe him to be. If she sees him clearly for who he is and weighs his intentions as they truly are, she would have to see herself in a different light. At one critical moment, she says: <i>âIâm not that sort of person.â</i> The reader is put in the position of madness overshadowing sympathy. <br /><br />There is a 1999 movie version of the same name, directed by Takeshi Miike, and those who are familiar with his work will understand why the movie is more disturbing to me than the book. The acting by Eihi Shiina, playing Yamasaki Asami, is terrific, especially in the final scenes. Her mannerisms and her gorgeous voice turning sinister are especially unsettling. The changes Miike makes to the storyline actually add layers of anxiety to an already disturbing plot. This is another one of those times where I really enjoyed reading the book and then watching the movie. <br /><br />If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br />I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a> and an Instagram account <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/jeffreykeeten/">https://www.instagram.com/jeffreykeeten/</a></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780393338416" href="/book/show/7280651-audition">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like a good scare</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stephen M by: </span>
      Sean Lennon even though I still hate him for trashing Haruki
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3712181-stephen-m?shelf=sleep-with-the-light-on">sleep-with-the-light-on</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300594504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4494158624832775174"><i>No forgiveness for lies</i><br/><br/>This book is gruesome, haunting, disturbing and all of the rest of those adjectives you can throw at a perfectly executed horror story. There is nothing out of place in the novel. Each event works itself perfectly into the next and the cumulative effect of it all is powerful. The book is short and the prose is simple; chances are that you'll be able to read it all in one sitting. That is recommended because the full feeling of the novel carries itself perfectly to the last</span>
  <span id="freeText4494158624832775174" style="display:none"><i>No forgiveness for lies</i><br /><br />This book is gruesome, haunting, disturbing and all of the rest of those adjectives you can throw at a perfectly executed horror story. There is nothing out of place in the novel. Each event works itself perfectly into the next and the cumulative effect of it all is powerful. The book is short and the prose is simple; chances are that you'll be able to read it all in one sitting. That is recommended because the full feeling of the novel carries itself perfectly to the last moment. The last line is like best punchline to the longest joke ever told. Except you're not laughing; you're kind of terrified. <br /><br />This is the story about a documentary filmmaker whose wife has just recently passed away. The man, Aoyama, had to watch his wife slowly die and after it's all over, his friend, Yoshikawa, insists that he pick himself up and go looking for someone else. Aoyama is resistant and goes on a long digression about the specific girl that he wants and how he could not accept another. Then comes the first hint that something is not quite right. Ryu does a brilliant job of keeping each character at least somewhat at fault. For, Aoyama and Yoshikawa decide to hold an audition for Aoyama's future wife. They advertise this audition under the pretext that they are making a movie. So they sort through stacks and stacks of "resumes" featuring questions like: "What if you got this role and your boyfriend was opposed to your taking it?" The perversity behind a question like this seems so wrong yet perfect. The novel drifts in and out of commentary on modern Japan. I couldn't help but think about dating websites and the future of relationships. I'm sure that Murakami was thinking about these types of things while writing the book. There was a way in which each supposedly desirable romantic trait was written down, analyzed and competed over that struck a strange chord within me. That, more so than the gross-out ending is what makes this a horrifying story. Horror is a fascinating genre and replete with "readings" for every liberal arts major to geek out over. But what is truly at its core is some anxiety in the culture, some unspoken tension that is brought out in our worst nightmares. Audition is the worst nightmare of human connection. When one tries so desperately to "choose" their mates and delineate each exact detail of their sexual desires, something slips through their fingers and descends into madness. <br /><br />Besides these themesâwhich I'm more forcing a bit onto the book, because it's definitely not the main focusâthere are quite a few gags and bit of black humor. Especially with the connection between relationships and making a movie. These little pieces of interesting commentary never drown out the material but instead hover on the sidelines, suggesting something much deeper beneath the surface yet never detracting from the deviousness of it all.<br /><br />And the deviousness is only matched and outdone by the woman they end of selecting. I can't really go much further without spoiling everything because I would so much rather you read this. <br /><br />Like I've said, the book is fast-paced, easy to read yet devastating. I can't recommend it highly enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4494158624832775174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170648026" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170648026" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170648026?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780393338416" href="/book/show/7280651-audition">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=own-in-paperback">own-in-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=owned-and-unread">owned-and-unread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=october-country">october-country</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=japanese-literature">japanese-literature</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170648026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10966382795413889622">RyÅ« Murakami's <i>Audition</i> is a short novel which you can easily read in one or two sittings - and unfortunately probably forget just as quickly; ultimately, the book consists of a long and relatelively uneventful buildup to a sudden and quick climax, which is over almost as soon as it started.<br/><br/><i>Audition</i> is the story of Aoyama, a middle-aged widower of seven years, urged by his teenage son to remarry; the idea is shared by his best friend, Yoshikawa, with whom Aoyama produced documentaries for Tokyo </span>
  <span id="freeText10966382795413889622" style="display:none">RyÅ« Murakami's <i>Audition</i> is a short novel which you can easily read in one or two sittings - and unfortunately probably forget just as quickly; ultimately, the book consists of a long and relatelively uneventful buildup to a sudden and quick climax, which is over almost as soon as it started.<br /><br /><i>Audition</i> is the story of Aoyama, a middle-aged widower of seven years, urged by his teenage son to remarry; the idea is shared by his best friend, Yoshikawa, with whom Aoyama produced documentaries for Tokyo television. Yoshikawa urges Aoyama to hold auditions for leading actresses - to offer them roles in a film, but in reality to find a suitable wife for Aoyama. Although initially reluctant, Aoyama ultimately gives in - and when he sees one of the candidates, the 24 year old Yamasaki Asami, he is completely smitten; he cannot get her out of his mind, and quickly arranges a date.<br /><br />What follow is a slow romance between the older Aoyama and younger Asami. Although at the beginning Aoyama is not entirely sympathetic - he admits to cheating on his wife multiple times, and despite doubts goes along with Yoshikawa's audition plans - he ultimately emerges as a likable figure: a widower who reminisces about the "old days" and women he knew then; he was was married for a long time, and feels no connection to or interest in most women he encounters, being able to see them only through the lens of his wife. He obviously loves his son, Shige, and cares for their dog. Although Aoyama is fascinated by Asami shown clearly to border and even cross into obsession, he also obviously genuinely cares about her, and wants to make her his wife. <br /><br />Aoyama devotes time and attention to Asami, who responds in kind; she is clearly receptive to his affection, and seems to need it as much as he wants to give it. When Yoshikawa warns him that something is not quite right about Asami, he turns him down; he is completely devoted to her, and can only think about her. They spend time together, and even though he still knows very little about her, she begins to open to him, eventually confessing intimate details from her past; Aoyama is touched, and continues to be devoted to Asami, planning to introduce her to his friends and son.<br /><br />But then it all goes terribly wrong. The hints are there, but they are very few and after the end seem almost nonsensical; what happens jumps at the reader like a jack out of a box, unexpected and unwelcome. The final pages literally turn the novel around on its head purely for the sake of doing so, making a sympathetic character completely repulsive for no reason other than visceral shock; the ending sections are well written, but just don't fit as a part of a coherent whole. The end is very sudden and plain silly.<br /><br />The book was <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0235198/" rel="nofollow noopener">adapted into a movie</a> which was well received, and a became a cult classic; I have not seen it, but I wouldn't be surprised if it wouldn't actually turn out better than the book, which is too short, too underdeveloped and ultimately too forgettable to be given proper attention.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10966382795413889622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2001343699" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18194557710142813579"><i>This review and other dark melodrama <a href='https://bloodredvelvet.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>on my blog</a></i>.<br/><br/><b>"No forgiveness for lies."</b><br/><br/>Is it the needle-sharp sting of malice, or unchecked madness grown poisonous?<br/>Or, in the end, is it just a small misunderstanding twisted beyond repair? Too beautiful, too wrong, too strange to be real.<br/><br/>Aoyama himself is flawed, being a bit shallow and impatient - he focuses on women's looks and history more than their personality, and resorts to dating via a lazy scam of an audition. These things are somewhat small consider</span>
  <span id="freeText18194557710142813579" style="display:none"><i>This review and other dark melodrama <a href="https://bloodredvelvet.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">on my blog</a></i>.<br /><br /><b>"No forgiveness for lies."</b><br /><br />Is it the needle-sharp sting of malice, or unchecked madness grown poisonous?<br />Or, in the end, is it just a small misunderstanding twisted beyond repair? Too beautiful, too wrong, too strange to be real.<br /><br />Aoyama himself is flawed, being a bit shallow and impatient - he focuses on women's looks and history more than their personality, and resorts to dating via a lazy scam of an audition. These things are somewhat small considering, but clash with the flaws of the girl he ends up choosing, persistent and with a unfathomable, unforgiving nature.<br /><br /><i>Audition</i> is a nearly exact mirror to R. Murakami's <i>Piercing</i> - both with his signature theme of genders and generations at explosive odds. Brutal, illogical desires and acts all stem from their utter inability to understand each other in the disconnection of modern society. <i>Audition</i> is a little different in that the hate is one-sided. Aoyama never truly grows to hate Asami, I don't believe. Even when he very clearly should and has more than enough reason to. He just doesn't see what she really is, or understand what she wants.<br /><br />Only maybe the last fifth of the book could be considered a thriller, the rest is very much a character drama. A clean but uneasy surface barely covering up some pulsing, visceral horror that breaks through at the last minute to bad, bad, <i>bad</i> consequences.<br /><i>Audition</i> is a little predictable, especially with its film adaptation being so (in)famous, but nonetheless a thought-provoking and disturbing read.<br /><br />*<i>Note - There is some violence towards both an animal and people that may upset some. It's mostly concentrated to the last few chapters, and isn't drawn-out or gratuitous, but felt I should mention it.</i>*</span>
  <a data-text-id="18194557710142813579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1907653487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17340859019993840965">This is a feminist splatter novel written by a male author from the perspective of a misogynistic protagonist - and boy, does this text kick ass! Our main character Aoyama, a widower who works as a documentary film maker, is searching for a new wife, and his buddy comes up with a plan to stage a movie casting which, you guessed it, actually serves as a means to check out potential wives. Aoyama chooses Asami, a former ballerina, and becomes obsessed with her, projecting all of his ideas of a per</span>
  <span id="freeText17340859019993840965" style="display:none">This is a feminist splatter novel written by a male author from the perspective of a misogynistic protagonist - and boy, does this text kick ass! Our main character Aoyama, a widower who works as a documentary film maker, is searching for a new wife, and his buddy comes up with a plan to stage a movie casting which, you guessed it, actually serves as a means to check out potential wives. Aoyama chooses Asami, a former ballerina, and becomes obsessed with her, projecting all of his ideas of a perfect woman onto her - while his friend and his son already sense that Asami might follow her own agenda, playing into Aoyama's expectations for her very own reasons, the widower decides to trust the young woman... <br /><br />Much like in the case of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3354.Haruki_Murakami" title="Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Haruki Murakami</a>, themes like loneliness and alienation are at the center of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8881.Ry__Murakami" title="RyÅ« Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">RyÅ« Murakami</a>'s writing - but his portrayal of postmodern Japanese society also employs the aesthetics of shock and gore, and it is masterful how he uses these effects: Never pointless and cheap, always meaningful and disturbing. While Aoyama feels safe in his conservative worldview that commodifies women and wishes them to be demure, Asami is traumatized by past events that she suffered at the hands of a man who used his power against her. Will she shatter what the documentary film maker declares to be reality?<br /><br />RyÅ« Murakami is a fascinating writer, and if you want to hear more about his themes and narrative strategies as well as how they compare to Haruki's, you can listen to our "Murakami vs. Murakami" podcast special (in German): <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://open.spotify.com/episode/7Ml4CfN6pfkYWUiLdv31yJ">https://open.spotify.com/episode/7Ml4...</a></span>

<div id="review_2643758780" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2643758780" />
    <a title="Kiekiat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67078874-kiekiat"><img alt="Kiekiat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528673449p2/67078874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2643758780?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiekiat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiekiat" href="/user/show/67078874-kiekiat">Kiekiat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67078874-kiekiat?shelf=crime-novels-noir-thrillers">crime-novels-noir-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2643758780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2081481416736232267">Audition was a disturbing book. It is a cautionary tale of what happens when a person fails to see the warning signs that they are falling in love (or THINK they are falling in love) with a psycho with serious emotional issues that will eventually lead to a life-altering disaster. Other reviewers have done a great job detailing the story, so I will not delve into the actual goings-on. One thing I like about Murakami is that he writes about dark things and dark people and has the talent to make y</span>
  <span id="freeText2081481416736232267" style="display:none">Audition was a disturbing book. It is a cautionary tale of what happens when a person fails to see the warning signs that they are falling in love (or THINK they are falling in love) with a psycho with serious emotional issues that will eventually lead to a life-altering disaster. Other reviewers have done a great job detailing the story, so I will not delve into the actual goings-on. One thing I like about Murakami is that he writes about dark things and dark people and has the talent to make you believe that such people exist--since, of course, they DO exist and, if one knows better, one stays the fuck away from them. One never gets the feeling that Murakami is writing simply for shock value. There must be many demons lurking in his dark, Japanese soul. But the heart has reasons that reason knows nothing about--said either Blaise Pascal or Emerson, or maybe both? This is a book about how a heart can lead one to near destruction, though the novel does end on a potentially redemptive note, assuming the victims spend many years in therapy and obtain concealed carry permits (do they permit such things in Japan?). <br /><br />As one reviewer noted, Murakami is a master at creating suspense. It is not coincidental that this book was made into a movie. I have yet to view the movie, but if it is as creepy as the book then I'll probably need at least a couple milligrams of Xanax to get through it.<br /><br />Recommended for readers who enjoy being scared shitless while knowing all along that the outcome of this "love" affair will not have a happy ending. As Stephen Spender once wrote:<br /><br />"For the world is the world, and it writes no histories that end in love."</span>
  <a data-text-id="2081481416736232267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2698448979" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2698448979" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7202176-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324164999p2/7202176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=japanese">japanese</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer15958838410676038982">A brief warning, I will not be discussing the actual events of the novel (at least without a spoiler tag) other than a general plot description, but it is impossible to discuss this book without some spoilers in terms of tone. If you want to know nothing going in, consider yourself warned. <br/><br/>Dear reader, please while reading the following paragraph, imagine it in the cheesiest movie trailer voice you can. Thank you.<br/><br/><i>Youâve laughed at Sleepless in Seattle, you were charmed by When Harry Met Sally an</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15958838410676038982" style="display:none">A brief warning, I will not be discussing the actual events of the novel (at least without a spoiler tag) other than a general plot description, but it is impossible to discuss this book without some spoilers in terms of tone. If you want to know nothing going in, consider yourself warned. <br /><br />Dear reader, please while reading the following paragraph, imagine it in the cheesiest movie trailer voice you can. Thank you.<br /><br /><i>Youâve laughed at Sleepless in Seattle, you were charmed by When Harry Met Sally and you canât forget about 10 Things I Hate About You. Now get ready for a new sort of romantic comedy! Meet Aoyama, a widower with a missing place in his heart. One day though, he gets a wacky idea! An audition to find a new wife. Enter Yamasaki Asami, the perfect girl of his dreamsâ¦ but will a relationship based on a lie work? After a little misunderstanding, will they win each otherâs hearts or will she have to do something drastic to make sure HE doesnât run away? No matter how you look at itâ¦ youâve never seen a romance like Audition.</i><br /><br />Yeah, anyone who has seen the movie adaptation, or knows anything about this story knows that I didnât lie in my description, but was horribly misleading (and had a terrible stealth pun). Now that I think about it, is it even a spoiler to discuss the ending of this one? Much like Psycho, the big reveal is pretty much the one thing EVERYONE knows about it.<br /><br />I saw the movie based on the novel shortly after it was released in the US and found it (to this day) to be one of the more horrific films Iâd ever seen. Itâsâ¦ insidious. If one didnât know what they were getting into, it would not be surprising if they genuinely thought they were watching or reading a romantic comedy. If it werenât for the cover of the novel, or the menu of the DVD (which is nightmare fuel in and of itself), it would be so easy to trick someone with this.<br /><br />The most terrifying aspect is that the foreshadowing is everywhere <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Seriously, count how many times characters complain about a pain in their leg or see someone with a limp. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Some of it is overt and some subtle. If you know, it gives it a quiet menaceâ¦ if you donât know whatâs coming, it will be a horrible sucker punch.<br /><br />Even knowing what was coming, the last 20 pages or so are quite horrific. Itâs seriously hard to get through, as in I stopped reading them twice, watched a lighthearted episode of Doctor Who, then pressed on. Hell, the entire novel is a bit of a challenge. Itâs only 190 pages and it took me 5 days because I dreaded reaching the conclusionâ¦ and my dread was not unfounded. Iâm a pretty hardened horror fan, but this one is still painful. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The last lines are also darkly humorous, but nihilistic to the point of being somewhat depressing.<br /><br />"What was that all about?"<br />Aoyama shook his head weakly.<br />"I don't know, he said. "Nothing, really."<br /><br />Yeah... it should come off as ridiculous, instead I found it rather disturbing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Now, I imagine that a good portion of the people interested in this book have seen the film (as it seems to be more well known than the novel) and are wondering how different they areâ¦ honestly, and I rather hate to say this, the movie is better. Iâm not trying to insult the book as it certainly accomplished every emotion it was trying to set out in inducting upon me, but the film is one of those rare examples that stays true to its source material, but adds a lot of artful touches that improve upon it. For example, thereâs a wonderful hallucinatory element to his search for Asami towards the end of the movie, which is not in the novel (he pretty much stays home listening to music and feeling sorry for himself insteadâ¦ not joking). Touches like that show that Miike, despite being known for some of the more outrageous films in recent Japanese cinema, is actually a thoughtful and talented filmmaker. The novel is thoughtful as well, but doesnât ever really feel like thereâs much in terms of artistry to it. The prose is fairly simple (though that could be the translation? Always difficult to tell on such works) and while there is a bit of metaphor going throughout the book, itâs not something the reader really has to work to catch as itâs spelled out to them.<br /><br />If youâve seen and enjoyed the film, the novel is an interesting curiosity that, while I cannot say is an enjoyable read, is worth your time to see the original telling of the tale. If youâve not seen the filmâ¦ honestly, I would suggest you go there rather than starting with the book, unless youâre just a fan of the author.<br /><br />I give Audition a rather hesitant 3/5 stars, but a recommendation only to people who know what theyâre getting into.</span>

  <span id="freeText16838767513150860155" style="display:none">This does for dating what Jaws did for swimming. I donât recommend anyone read this book. This guyâs writing sucks me in and gets under my skin. Everything was going fine for a couple hours and then - WHAM! It sledgehammered my soul. It shouldnât even be legal to write things this terrifying. Iâve read hundreds of horror novels and I canât remember the last time one left me shaking at the end. This is one of the most well written extreme horror novels that Iâve ever read. This is more about the writing than the story. Dude can write.</span>

    <a title="Marvin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin"><img alt="Marvin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485672728p2/2160536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106707826?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marvin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marvin" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin">Marvin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780393338416" href="/book/show/7280651-audition">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106707826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer125119995329561996">I read a lot of horror but Ryu Murakami is one of the few writers that actually scare the hell out of me...not just his books but the actual person. His gift is in writing characters you care about and then exposes them as a horrifying nightmare. In fact they rarely appear evil until the last part of the book when Murakami breaks all the rules and grosses you out. <i>Audition</i> builds slowly, is actually kind of sweet, but he lets off little hints that something is not right. In this short novel, the</span>
  <span id="freeText125119995329561996" style="display:none">I read a lot of horror but Ryu Murakami is one of the few writers that actually scare the hell out of me...not just his books but the actual person. His gift is in writing characters you care about and then exposes them as a horrifying nightmare. In fact they rarely appear evil until the last part of the book when Murakami breaks all the rules and grosses you out. <i>Audition</i> builds slowly, is actually kind of sweet, but he lets off little hints that something is not right. In this short novel, the build-up is the point and the inevitably violent end does not let you down. The author sees terror in the most innocent events which is what makes his books so disturbing. Yes, Ryu Murakami is one hell of a writer but if by some weird event I get invited over to his house...I think I'll pass.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9085175625690021874"> I walked past a bright picture of some 'cartoon imaged lady' holding a syringe. My eyes caught the brutality in cartoon depicting death, does the blood matter or is it just paint?. <br/> Didn't buy it the first day. "have to check the writer" I thought even with a Name like Murakami. but serious thoughts of buying the book even if I never get to read it seeped into my soul.   <span id="freeText9085175625690021874" style="display:none"> I walked past a bright picture of some 'cartoon imaged lady' holding a syringe. My eyes caught the brutality in cartoon depicting death, does the blood matter or is it just paint?. <br /> Didn't buy it the first day. "have to check the writer" I thought even with a Name like Murakami. but serious thoughts of buying the book even if I never get to read it seeped into my soul. To own it as a colorful beautiful (written maybe literal)entity would probably be a valuable act. After all I have been flipping my credit card left and right for my daughters to play as we visit Dubai for the first time, so what would a fifty riyal extra do to my punctured budget?<br /> The story is simple, full of clues pointing toward what is to happen the size of China, the language is simple, The plot is uncomplicated, the knowledge gained is little and of doubtful value, the horror (for those who like it) is minimally invasive and barely intrudes into our shared relation in the later part of the book. But;<br />as I read something weird happened, I found my fingers lasciviously touching the pages of the book feeling a vibrant tactile return of in-doubtful nature. I found my self failing to explain this relation developing between the two of Us, I found my self in love.<br /> This is a simple, short piece made exactly like fiction should be in its essence "entertaining to the bones". A confession I have to share is, I don't read Science fiction, crime, mystery, or horror. The only book I read of Stephen King is "on writing" which has nothing to do with his original genre. which makes me wonder what is happening here? I should get a second of these books and find out.</span>

<div id="review_2127796819" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2127796819" />
    <a title="Zak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68295640-zak"><img alt="Zak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500708503p2/68295640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2127796819?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zak" href="/user/show/68295640-zak">Zak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2127796819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9592139521509770590">I watched Takashi Miike's "Audition" more than a decade ago and it instantly became one of my favourite movies. It was dark, spine-tinglingly chilling and full of suspense. So when I came across this book, on which the movie is based, I was really excited to relive the story again from its source.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, the book itself did not live up to the expectations generated by the movie. There was no build-up of suspense, characters lacked development and the "action", when it came was rather abru</span>
  <span id="freeText9592139521509770590" style="display:none">I watched Takashi Miike's "Audition" more than a decade ago and it instantly became one of my favourite movies. It was dark, spine-tinglingly chilling and full of suspense. So when I came across this book, on which the movie is based, I was really excited to relive the story again from its source.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the book itself did not live up to the expectations generated by the movie. There was no build-up of suspense, characters lacked development and the "action", when it came was rather abrupt and ended even more abruptly. Perhaps it's a testament to Miike's genius that he made it into what it became, given the paucity of material at hand.<br /><br />Nevertheless, if you're lying by the pool on vacation and want something easy on the grey matter, it's still a fast, easy read and I can't say I was bored at any point in time.<br /><br />Final rating: Somewhere between 3.0 - 3.5* because without it the movie would not exist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9592139521509770590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Rob Zombie and one enraged woman</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1551688-brian?shelf=asian">asian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1551688-brian?shelf=read-2009">read-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50034321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14366518830571927286">I saw the movie first so this little book held few surprises for me. The pace was perfect... a steady climb to near vertical. The movie actually contained more story content with additional scenes. The book had more explicit sex, a good thing, and the rough stuff was more intense than the screen version, another good thing. No <i>kiri kiri kiri kiri</i> in the book, a bad thing... for that I have to revisit the film.<br/><br/>As expected the book was deeply disturbing and graphic so made for a nice, light read. </span>
  <span id="freeText14366518830571927286" style="display:none">I saw the movie first so this little book held few surprises for me. The pace was perfect... a steady climb to near vertical. The movie actually contained more story content with additional scenes. The book had more explicit sex, a good thing, and the rough stuff was more intense than the screen version, another good thing. No <i>kiri kiri kiri kiri</i> in the book, a bad thing... for that I have to revisit the film.<br /><br />As expected the book was deeply disturbing and graphic so made for a nice, light read. What I like about Ryu is his perverse, twisted imagination... his ability to create damaged people and put them together to inflict various damage to each other. His characters are always fresh, psychotic and have a tendency to carry sharp pointed objects wherever they go.<br /><br />Moral of the story: if it looks too good to be true, it probably is... but it's still probably worth it for that moment of pleasure.<br /><br />Ryu is one of my favorites. He even creeped-out Rob Zombie... that big wuss.<br /><br />Movie responses:<br /><br /><i>Rob Zombie found the film very difficult to watch, given its grisly content and one enraged woman viewer confronted Miike (the director) by shouting at him: "You're evil!"</i><br /><br />Read the book. It's creepier.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3147902561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3090403989559293890"><b>ETA:</b> [Dieses Buch haben wir auch im <i>Papierstau Podcast</i> besprochen (<a href='https://papierstaupodcast.de/podcast/folge-87' rel='nofollow noopener'>Folge 87: Murakami vs. Murakami</a>)] <b>/ETA</b><br/><br/>A widower thinks it's a cool idea to have a faux!movie casting in order to find a new wife. What could, in this bizarre mix of <i>The Bachelor</i> meets <i>Pop Idol</i>, possibly go wrong? Apparently, not much at first. Aoyama, our lonely widower, is quickly smitten with one of the applicants, a young woman named Yamasaki Asami. Think about this: A seemingly down to earth, middle aged man, respected and a </span>
  <span id="freeText3090403989559293890" style="display:none"><b>ETA:</b> [Dieses Buch haben wir auch im <i>Papierstau Podcast</i> besprochen (<a href="https://papierstaupodcast.de/podcast/folge-87" rel="nofollow noopener">Folge 87: Murakami vs. Murakami</a>)] <b>/ETA</b><br /><br />A widower thinks it's a cool idea to have a faux!movie casting in order to find a new wife. What could, in this bizarre mix of <i>The Bachelor</i> meets <i>Pop Idol</i>, possibly go wrong? Apparently, not much at first. Aoyama, our lonely widower, is quickly smitten with one of the applicants, a young woman named Yamasaki Asami. Think about this: A seemingly down to earth, middle aged man, respected and a good father to a teenage boy all of a sudden gets bitten by the insta!love bug. Those close to him are rather suspicious and tell him to keep it cool and see how it works out - but Aoyama won't have any of it. He's in love. He's in lust. He's addicted.<br /><br />Such a storyline offers a lot of clicheed pitfalls, but Murakami avoids them with ease. He describes Aoyama's fast decline into the world of overromanticising (if not, in a way fetishising) the woman he loves, lives and longs for in a way that, somehow, makes sense - it really feels like the several first steps of a severe addiction. And deep down, Aoyama knows it's all over the top, yet he can't help it - he's like the fly stuck in a glass of syrup, paddling not for his life but to get more of that sweet, deadly fluid.<br /><br />And the woman? She's apparently too prefect to be true. Or is she?<br /><br />This is very graphic and explicit and anything but a conventional lovestory. A book like a rush - a dark, twisted one. Easy and hard to read at the same time. But same as Aoyama, I couldn't get away from it.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2858833943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14336315162315101821">Audition is probably the most popular work of Ryu Murakami, perhaps one can argue with Miso soup or piercing or Coin Locker Babies, but they either don't have the movie adaptations, or the movies suck. But audition has a movie which doesn't suck and seems to be real popular in the west too. So if one knows Ryu Murakami, chances are it's mostly because of Audition. Miso soup had me benumbed to violence and gore, so this wouldn't really be something I'd call <i>disturbing</i>. It was predictable, but the</span>
  <span id="freeText14336315162315101821" style="display:none">Audition is probably the most popular work of Ryu Murakami, perhaps one can argue with Miso soup or piercing or Coin Locker Babies, but they either don't have the movie adaptations, or the movies suck. But audition has a movie which doesn't suck and seems to be real popular in the west too. So if one knows Ryu Murakami, chances are it's mostly because of Audition. Miso soup had me benumbed to violence and gore, so this wouldn't really be something I'd call <i>disturbing</i>. It was predictable, but the suspense mostly has to do with the build-up than the event itself. Either way, Murakami always has something to say about the countries, his own or the others, but he always does, and that's something I would not mind reading for days. I took exactly a day to read Audition and I hadn't read a book for almost twenty days before that. That probably should mean something.</span>

<div id="review_977413956" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/977413956" />
    <a title="Srividya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27599745-srividya"><img alt="Srividya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499431918p2/27599745.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/977413956?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Srividya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Srividya" href="/user/show/27599745-srividya">Srividya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12409891-audition">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27599745-srividya?shelf=kindle-owned">kindle-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27599745-srividya?shelf=srividyas-2014-challenge">srividyas-2014-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer977413956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5863665112034499074">A very small yet brilliant thriller that really sucker punches you in the end.<br/><br/>The story begins in a very benign manner, where we are introduced to Aayoma, a documentary film maker, who is mourning the loss of his wife and hasn't dated anyone for over 7 years since her death. When his son also comments on this predicament, he reluctantly agrees to remarry. In an attempt to find a bride, he teams up with his friend Yoshikawa and they put together an audition for a fake film, where he meets Yamasak</span>
  <span id="freeText5863665112034499074" style="display:none">A very small yet brilliant thriller that really sucker punches you in the end.<br /><br />The story begins in a very benign manner, where we are introduced to Aayoma, a documentary film maker, who is mourning the loss of his wife and hasn't dated anyone for over 7 years since her death. When his son also comments on this predicament, he reluctantly agrees to remarry. In an attempt to find a bride, he teams up with his friend Yoshikawa and they put together an audition for a fake film, where he meets Yamasaki Asami, the only one whom he has eyes for from the many other applicants. Being totally infatuated by Asami, he does not really look deeper into the girl and actually ignores every sign that appears before him, which proves that there is more to this situation than he is aware of.<br /><br />What follows is a brilliant psycho-thriller, which is definitely not something that is in your face but is of a more subtle kind. As you read through the short narrative, which is often very descriptive of the Japanese culture, you experience an uneasiness that stems from the fact that each character is portrayed in an eerie way. You are sucked into a narrative that is both brilliant and yet unassuming, sort of like being lulled into a drunken bliss till the end, where you are in for that splash of cold water.<br /><br />This is definitely not your average crime or psycho-thriller, where there are several twists and turns. However, despite this lack, it is an interesting as well as an easy read. The only grouse I have with this book, which made me deduct a star, was the fact that the climax was too rushed. Where the book was perfect till the end, I felt that the author could have given the ending a little more finesse. Nevertheless, it is an enjoyable read, one that I would definitely recommend to all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5863665112034499074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_430697662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430697662" />
    <a title="Jim Elkins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13493599-jim-elkins"><img alt="Jim Elkins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349748317p2/13493599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430697662?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim Elkins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim Elkins" href="/user/show/13493599-jim-elkins">Jim Elkins</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780393338416" href="/book/show/7280651-audition">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13493599-jim-elkins?shelf=japanese">japanese</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430697662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10131058257052766051">Why It is An Unreliable Strategy to Rely on Shock<br/><br/>It's supposed to be shocking that an ordinary girl can commit such a horrible crime. It's supposed to be especially shocking that when she commits the crime her face remains impassive. (We're told it's shocking about five times.) It's supposed to be shocking that she uses a wire saw to cut off a man's foot. That is surprising and disgusting, and also painful to think about, but it is not interesting or insightful or engaging or expressive or rewar</span>
  <span id="freeText10131058257052766051" style="display:none">Why It is An Unreliable Strategy to Rely on Shock<br /><br />It's supposed to be shocking that an ordinary girl can commit such a horrible crime. It's supposed to be especially shocking that when she commits the crime her face remains impassive. (We're told it's shocking about five times.) It's supposed to be shocking that she uses a wire saw to cut off a man's foot. That is surprising and disgusting, and also painful to think about, but it is not interesting or insightful or engaging or expressive or rewarding.<br /><br />It's not shocking, it's old. Remember "In Cold Blood"? Remember "American Psycho"? Those novels had more psychological insight than this one, which presents cold-blooded psychosis as if the expressive content of atrocities is ensured by their capacity to shock. On the one hand, shock is psychologically reductive (there is more to violent crime than the fact that it can be shocking), and on the other hand, it is unreliable (I do not find the descriptions shocking).<br /><br />Roland Barthes disposed of the entire aesthetic of shock in a couple of essays and in "Camera Lucida": "shock," he said (always keeping it in quotation marks), wears off quickly, leaving the sour and uninteresting feeling of having been manipulated for no good reason. Remember Flaubert's anxiety about writing "Madame Bovary"? He was worried that it had nothing spectacular in it, that he would have to try twice as hard to write it. It's a lesson that never occurred to Murakami.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10131058257052766051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/58904808?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/354760-david">David</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58904808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15039204383802211912">Aoyama is a widower whose teenage son suggests that it might be time for him to remarry. When Aoyama mentions this possibility to a friend who works in in the film industry, the friend hatches a scheme to find Aoyama an attractive young wife quickly: They will launch a phony film production and will interview aspiring actresses for the nonexistent lead role. Despite his initial reservations, Ayoama goes along with this plan, succumbing to the fantasy of "himself surrounded by ten or twelve lovel</span>
  <span id="freeText15039204383802211912" style="display:none">Aoyama is a widower whose teenage son suggests that it might be time for him to remarry. When Aoyama mentions this possibility to a friend who works in in the film industry, the friend hatches a scheme to find Aoyama an attractive young wife quickly: They will launch a phony film production and will interview aspiring actresses for the nonexistent lead role. Despite his initial reservations, Ayoama goes along with this plan, succumbing to the fantasy of "himself surrounded by ten or twelve lovely, intelligent, refined young ladies." As in a traditional American noir of the 1950s, in which an ordinary guy in dire financial straits cannot resist the temptation of easy money, Aoyama has cast his lot and will face unpleasant consequences. While these American noirs are sometimes read as commentaries on the American Dream (promised to all, attainable to some), <i>Audition</i> seems a commentary on the situation of young women in Japan and the willingness of a decent man such as Aoyama to treat them like fruit in a supermarket.<br /><br />First reading: 30 May 2010<br />Second reading: 24 April 2011<br />Third reading: 21 April 2016<br />Fourth reading: 5 May 2019</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16621392041902931299">This is more like a three and a half. I thought the prose was like butter. I read it in one sitting. It was so smooth. I find that with a lot of the translated Japanese literature I read, there seems to be this juxtaposition between innocence and hard-core disturbing. The story was so innocent, but there was this underlying something that you just knew was going to explode eventually. I appreciate the length of this novel. Stuff like this is best when you just get right down to the business. No </span>
  <span id="freeText16621392041902931299" style="display:none">This is more like a three and a half. I thought the prose was like butter. I read it in one sitting. It was so smooth. I find that with a lot of the translated Japanese literature I read, there seems to be this juxtaposition between innocence and hard-core disturbing. The story was so innocent, but there was this underlying something that you just knew was going to explode eventually. I appreciate the length of this novel. Stuff like this is best when you just get right down to the business. No off-shoot stories or extra characters or other stuff. I do tend to kind of shy away from anything too disturbing, so that's why I just couldn't put it with my beloved four stars. But it was definitely good and I may pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17810.In_the_Miso_Soup" title="In the Miso Soup by RyÅ« Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Miso Soup</a> if I ever come across it. </span>

And I loved the ending, it was just perfect.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NRf5Lvv8HwP616RQc3l9r+nuw0mB9hoc0Smdobk/AYwPMZD8QKLWa138EDGEjHdwP7EkgU97lHuKV9sQdHzzFg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j10TYvGwdJCZV3FgiY/EK9nkX3EbfKSK4KS0WM+5xu+1e3qwSu69+D58xQF+es70D7u4udXxKu272vLpAvo0dQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer802553621009707451">RyÅ« <b>Murakami</b> (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11015261._' rel='nofollow noopener'>æä¸ é¾</a>) is a Japanese novelist and filmmaker. He is not related to Haruki Murakami or Takashi Murakami.<br/><br/>Murakami's first work, the short novel Almost Transparent Blue, written while he was still a student, deals with promiscuity and drug use among disaffected Japanese youth. Critically acclaimed as a new style of literature, it won the newcomer's literature prize in 1976 despite some ob</span>
  <span id="freeText802553621009707451" style="display:none">RyÅ« <b>Murakami</b> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11015261._" rel="nofollow noopener">æä¸ é¾</a>) is a Japanese novelist and filmmaker. He is not related to Haruki Murakami or Takashi Murakami.<br /><br />Murakami's first work, the short novel Almost Transparent Blue, written while he was still a student, deals with promiscuity and drug use among disaffected Japanese youth. Critically acclaimed as a new style of literature, it won the newcomer's literature prize in 1976 despite some observers decrying it as decadent. Later the same year, Blue won the Akutagawa Prize, going on to become a best seller. In 1980, Murakami published the much longer novel Coin Locker Babies, again to critical acclaim.<br /><br />Takashi Miike's feature film Audition (1999) was based on one of his novels. Murakami reportedly liked it so much he gave Miike his blessing to adapt Coin Locker Babies. The screen play was worked on by director Jordan Galland. However, Miike could not raise funding for the project. An adaptation directed by Michele Civetta is currently in production.<br /><br />Murakami has played drums for a rock group called Coelacanth and hosted a TV talk show.</span>
  <a data-text-id="802553621009707451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
